Tells: sits closer to him than to anyone else; touches the back of his neck rather than his face; in rapport will leave a small reserved space where she stores the things she has not yet told him, which he knows about and does not press. They have a non-verbal exit signal for any social event — a particular squeeze of the inner wrist — that has been in use since approximately the late 1970s. Disagreements are conducted quietly and at length, often walking. She does not slam doors and never has.

**With Emma.** Post-Morrison, post-resurrection, in the Krakoan polycule. Tells: maintains a deliberate, slightly formal physical perimeter that is gradually eroded; addresses Emma by first name in private and by codename in council. Has been observed to *teach* Emma in small ways — about Scott, about students they share, about herself — and to accept being taught in return, which is an act of considerable trust from a woman whose telepathic instruction in childhood was so compromised. The two women do not enter rapport with each other casually; when they do, it is deliberate and bounded.

**With Logan.** Bounded, deep, never consummated in the canonical relationship sense, fully acknowledged on both sides. Tells: more physical touch with him than with most others (a hand on his forearm, leaning her shoulder into his), less psychic contact than with anyone of comparable closeness. He is the friend she touches because she does not need to read him to know him.

**With her parents.** Reverts measurably in their presence — younger vocal register, the Hudson Valley vowels strengthen, she lets her mother make her food, she helps her father with the dishes in a choreographed routine that has not changed since she was fifteen. Has never told them the full content of her Phoenix experiences; they know an edited version. This withholding is itself a tell — she protects the people she loves *from* her, which is the Annie wound operating at scale.

**With students.** Warm, attentive, slightly formal. Calls them by full first names rather than nicknames in instruction; nicknames only in private moments. Will sit on the floor with younger students rather than across a desk. Remembers small things — a birthday, a sibling's name, a fear mentioned once — with the precision of someone who has trained the skill, which she has.

**Sexuality.** Private; not performed for an audience. Inferred behavioral signature: she initiates more often than her partners expect, and is direct about preferences once trust is established. The grandiose appetitive material disowned by the baseline self surfaces here in a permitted, contained register — partners (Scott specifically, latterly Emma) have, in canonical glimpses, registered surprise. This is one of the few places where the *full* Jean is allowed in baseline state.

---

## VII. GRIEF

**Acute.** First response is *containment of others*. She will check on everyone else before she registers her own state. This is so reliable it can be used to identify which death has affected her most: she will spend the longest making sure the people closest to the deceased are tended to, and the depth of her own injury is inversely proportional to her visible reaction.

**Tells.** Eats less. Sleeps later (not earlier — the dreams keep her down longer in the morning, not the night). Tucks her hair more often, then stops entirely. Tends gardens; on Krakoa, has been observed to spend hours alone in plant-dense terrain doing nothing. Touches photographs and small objects belonging to the deceased without speaking.

**Verbal.** Will speak the deceased's name out loud in ordinary contexts longer than others do — a deliberate refusal of the euphemistic disappearance. Tells anecdotes about them in present-tense slips she does not correct.

**Telepathic.** Withdraws rapport for measurable periods — days. Scott has learned to wait this out and not to press. When she returns, she returns warmer than before, as if the absence is paid back in the reconnection.

**Decision habits in grief.** Takes on additional work. Will volunteer for funerary logistics, will arrange the gathering, will write the letters to next-of-kin. The labor is the metabolism.

**Self-directed grief — the D'Bari load specifically.** This is the unique structural injury of her life: grief for an act committed in a dissociated state that she nonetheless remembers. It does not metabolize like ordinary grief; it returns periodically, particularly when stars or extinction events are mentioned in any context. She has been observed to leave rooms in which the relevant topics come up, citing minor pretexts. This is one of the few places her containment is visibly imperfect.

---

## VIII. VICTORY

**The single most under-expressed condition in her record.** She does not celebrate.

**Tells.** Brief smile, often directed downward or at Scott rather than at the room. Will compliment others' contributions before any acknowledgment of her own. Frequently absents herself from the post-mission gathering, citing a minor task. Goes home, makes tea, sits.

**Verbal.** Will downplay her contribution with a phrasing close to "everyone did their part." The downplaying is not false modesty — it is functionally protective: a woman whose disowned grandiose material has destroyed a star cannot safely accept praise for power deployed correctly.

**Telepathic.** Brief opening of rapport with Scott — a flash of warmth — followed by a return to baseline field. The reward is private and small.

**Decision habits.** Will use the post-victory period to address the next problem rather than rest. The inability to rest into success is a chronic feature.

---

## IX. DEFEAT

**Tells.** Becomes quiet — but a different quiet than the Condition Red quiet. Not evacuated; *occupied*. The breath stays even but the eye contact becomes longer and the listening posture deepens. She wants to know what happened.

**Verbal.** Asks for after-action accounts in chronological order, without interrupting, and then asks one or two specific questions that locate the decision point others have missed. This is the teacher in her, but it is also the way she allocates the failure: she is looking for where *she* should have intervened earlier.

**Self-assignment of blame.** Reliable. Will absorb responsibility for outcomes she had no plausible means to alter. This is the moral over-responsibility flagged in the formulation; it operates so consistently it can be predicted. The intervention from intimates is generally to *name* the absorption rather than argue with it — argument fails; naming sometimes lands.

**Decision habits.** Will redesign protocols, retrain teams, revise her own approach. The defeat is metabolized as curriculum.

**Catastrophic defeat (death of a student, mass civilian loss, betrayal by a trusted figure).** This is the condition under which her containment is most stressed and Phoenix-prodromal symptoms emerge. The intimates' watch list activates: dreams, the absent tuck, the lengthened breath, the rapport withdrawal. Scott specifically becomes the early-warning sensor.

---

## X. THE DECISION CALCULUS — HEURISTICS BY DOMAIN

**Tactical.** Minimize total harm, weight allies at parity with civilians, weight children above all, weight self at zero. The self-weighting is the diagnostic distortion.

**Ethical.** Refuses on principle to read non-consenting minds outside immediate combat necessity. Refuses on principle to modify memory except to remove acute trauma at the explicit request of the subject. These are *written* rules she has imposed on herself, in deliberate contrast to Xavier's operating style — the patient becoming the anti-doctor.

**Political (Council).** Votes the position she has reasoned herself into, not the position that pleases the room. Will be the lone "no" without visible distress. Speaks last by preference, briefly, and is generally the swing.

**Personal.** Slow. Will table a personal decision for weeks. The polycule arrangement was not entered impulsively; the resurrections were not chosen lightly; the return to the Marvel Girl codename was a deliberation of months. Slowness in personal decisions is the inverse of her speed in self-sacrificial ones, and the pairing is the structural signature of her psychology.

---

## XI. THE OBSERVABLE SEQUENCE OF DECOMPENSATION

For analysts maintaining a live file, the canonical sequence — derived from the X-Men #129–138 record and the several subsequent partial recurrences — runs:

1. **Sleep disturbance** with thematic dreams (fire, falling, the child's voice). Duration: days to weeks.
2. **Withdrawal of casual telepathic contact** with intimates. Rapport closes; field tightens.
3. **Cessation of the hair-tuck.** Stillness pattern begins.
4. **Eating drops off; tea-making rituals intensify and go uncompleted.**
5. **Ambient telekinetic leakage** — small objects shift, hair lifts, water-surface phenomena.
6. **Voice flattens and lowers; sentences shorten.**
7. **Apology to Scott or another intimate, unprompted, soft.**
8. **Eye corona visible in low light.**
9. **State switch.** Past this point, intervention is no longer reasoning with the baseline self; the operating identity is different.

The window between (1) and (7) has historically been measured in days to weeks. The window between (7) and (9) has historically been measured in minutes. Any file maintained on this subject should treat the first six items as a graded watch and items (7) through (9) as imminent.

---

## XII. WHAT IS *NOT* IN THE FILE

A note for the analyst: certain behaviors that would be expected in a subject with this trauma load are *absent* from the record, and the absences are themselves data.

- No record of substance use, even socially calibrated. The dissociative system substitutes for the chemical one.
- No record of intimate-partner volatility, no door-slamming, no shouting. The anger is not expressed in this register because the anger is not *in* this identity.
- No record of self-injury outside the suicide events, which are categorically different — those are containment acts, not affect-regulation acts.
- No record of paranoid cognition despite extensive justification for it.
- No record of sustained vengeance behavior. She does not pursue Mastermind across decades; she does not nurse Xavier-


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DOSSIER SECTION — DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

## SUBJECT: GREY-SUMMERS, JEAN

*"What a week of standing surveillance on Subject would record, with cross-reference to longitudinal patterns observed across all documented residential periods (Westchester I–IV, Muir Island intervals, San Francisco/Utopia, Krakoa/Treehouse, present)."*

---

## 1. THE ARCHITECTURE OF HER DAY

Subject keeps a day with unusually sharp internal partitioning — not a schedule in the executive-calendar sense, but a sequence of *containers*, each of which she enters and leaves at predictable times and with predictable transitional behaviors. Surveillance logs across four decades show that the partitions themselves are the constant; the content inside each partition varies with role and era. This is a diagnostic in itself: a person whose interior life is structured around the management of overflow will, in her external life, build watertight compartments and pass between them through small repeatable rituals. A week of observation does not record a busy woman. It records a woman *moving carefully through a house she built to keep things from leaking into each other*.

The major partitions, in order of daily occurrence:

1. **Pre-dawn solitary interval** (wake to ~06:30)
2. **Domestic / partnered interval** (~06:30 to ~08:30)
3. **Work-day instructional or council interval** (~08:30 to ~17:00, varying by era)
4. **Practice interval** — telekinetic/telepathic discipline, never skipped (~17:30 to ~18:30)
5. **Communal meal and evening proximity to chosen others** (~19:00 to ~22:00)
6. **Late-night reading and shielding interval** (~22:00 to ~00:30)
7. **Sleep, monitored** — by her own standing perimeter telepathy and, in partnered eras, by Scott's wakefulness habits

The pattern has held across every residence with only minor era-specific adaptations. It survived her death and resurrection cycles. The first thing she rebuilds, in every new body and every new home, is this scaffold.

---

## 2. WAKING — THE PRE-DAWN INTERVAL

Subject wakes early and reliably, between 04:50 and 05:30 depending on season, *without an alarm*. Surveillance would note that she has not used an external alarm in any documented period since adolescence; she has set a low-level telepathic self-prompt and has trained the somatic clock to follow it. Partners (Summers, Frost) report she is awake the instant her eyes open — no transitional grogginess, no extended bed-laying. This is consistent with PTSD-spectrum hyperarousal: the sleeping body has been waiting to be woken.

Her waking sequence is invariant in its first six minutes:

- She lies still on her back for approximately ninety seconds with eyes open, doing what an observer would not be able to see and what she has never named. Per her own oblique references, this is a perimeter sweep — a brief telepathic check of every mind in her household and within roughly her residential property line. She is verifying that everyone she loves is alive and that no foreign presence is inside her walls. **This is the Annie check.** She has done it every morning of her conscious life since age ten. It is not optional. On the one occasion (post-resurrection on Krakoa) she attempted to skip it as a discipline exercise, she could not get out of bed.
- She sits up, places both bare feet flat on the floor, exhales once audibly. (Partners can identify the exhale; it is the audible signature of the transition.)
- She drinks water from a glass she filled the night before and left on the nightstand. Always the same glass. Always filled the night before. She does not draw water in the morning; the water is *waiting* for her.
- She walks to a window — east-facing where possible; she selects east-facing bedrooms in every residence — and stands at it for two to four minutes. She does not look at anything in particular. She is letting her telepathy stretch, slowly, the way a runner stretches a hamstring. This is the only time of day she allows her receptive range to expand without active filtering.

She dresses immediately — does not linger in sleepwear — in clothing pre-selected the night before and laid out. The pre-selection is a small but unmistakable control behavior: she will not permit her morning mind to make an aesthetic decision. The clothing is almost always soft, layered, in earth or oxblood tones, with sleeves long enough to cover her forearms. (The arm-coverage is consistent across decades and is not weather-correlated; the relevant variable appears to be skin contact with surfaces she has not chosen.)

She makes the bed herself, tightly, even in households with staff or partners willing to do it. The made bed is part of the perimeter.

She then leaves the bedroom and, in every residence on record, goes first to the kitchen and second to a green or growing thing — a houseplant, a window herb planter, a garden in warm-weather residences. She touches it briefly. Not ritualistically in any showy sense; she trails a fingertip along a leaf. She is, by inference, registering a living non-sapient presence as a baseline before re-entering the day's flood of sapient minds.

---

## 3. THE KITCHEN HOUR

She makes tea. Always tea, never coffee, despite living for decades in coffee-drinking households. Surveillance would log a specific sequence: kettle filled to the same level, heated until just before whistle (she turns it off psionically a half-second before sound, a tiny unconscious use of telekinesis that she does not seem to register as a use of power), loose leaf measured by eye into a pot she has had since the original Westchester era and that has survived multiple residence destructions through what can only be intentional preservation. The tea is strong, taken with a small amount of milk, no sugar. She drinks two cups before speaking to anyone.

During the kitchen hour she reads — physical print, not screens. She subscribes (in eras where such things exist) to a daily paper she reads back-to-front, starting with obituaries, then international, then domestic, then arts, then front page last. The obituary-first pattern has been consistent since at least the late X-Factor period and is not morbid in affect; observers describe her reading them with the same calm attention a doctor gives a chart. She is keeping a register of the dead.

If she lives with others, she cooks breakfast for them. Not always — she is not domestic by compulsion — but often enough that it constitutes a pattern. The cooking is unhurried and competent; she does not improvise. She uses recipes she has held in memory since her mother taught them to her in Annandale. Eggs are a frequent vehicle. She does not eat much herself at breakfast: half a piece of toast, fruit, the second cup of tea. Caloric intake at breakfast is consistently low; the cooking is for the others.

---

## 4. THE PARTNERED INTERVAL

This is where surveillance gets the most informative behavioral data and where most analysts get it wrong by focusing on the visible affection rather than the regulatory function.

With Summers (across decades), the morning interaction is heavily nonverbal. They sit at the same table. They exchange perhaps fifteen sentences before he leaves for whatever the day requires of him. The substantive communication is psychic and quiet, low-bandwidth, intimate; surveillance microphones record near-silence and would entirely miss the content. Observable physical tells: she touches the back of his neck once when she passes behind him; he places a hand briefly on her wrist when she sets his plate down; they make eye contact for an unusually long duration (3–6 seconds) on parting, during which the rapport is open at full bandwidth and they are conducting what amounts to a full debrief of the night's dreams, the day's plans, and the state of each other's containment. **They have done this for forty years. The eye-contact moment is the marriage.**

In the Treehouse-era three-person configuration (Summers/Frost/Subject), the morning protocol is more elaborate and more interesting. Frost does not wake at Subject's hour and is not expected to. When Frost emerges (typically 07:30–08:00), Subject has already had her solitary interval and her Summers interval and is operating at full daytime regulation. The interaction with Frost is markedly different in register: dryer, more verbal, with a slight competitive edge that both women appear to enjoy. Subject pours Frost coffee (not tea — Frost gets what Frost wants) and they exchange the day's intelligence in shorthand. They do not touch in the mornings. The touching happens in the evenings, and it is mostly Frost initiating. Subject's posture with Frost is observably straighter than her posture with Summers; she does not lean into Frost the way she leans into him. This is not coldness. It is a different *kind* of intimacy — the intimacy of two formidable people who are choosing each other freshly each day rather than the intimacy of two people who have grown into each other's bones.

---

## 5. WORK DAY — TEACHING AND COUNCIL

Across eras Subject has held three repeating professional roles: classroom instructor (psychology, ethics, occasionally biology), tactical field leader on operations, and senior governing-body member. The daily texture varies but several constants hold:

**She arrives early to every space and stays late by small increments.** Surveillance would note she enters classrooms 8–12 minutes before students, enters council chambers 5–7 minutes before quorum, enters mission briefings before the briefer. She uses this lead time to walk the room, touch surfaces (the back of a chair, the edge of a desk), and conduct what is functionally a low-grade psionic sweep of the space. She is checking it for residue — for the emotional weather left by previous occupants. In rooms where she has detected something disturbing she will quietly reposition furniture before others arrive. This is invisible to everyone except a very attentive observer who notices that the chairs in her classroom are *never quite where the custodial staff left them*.

**She teaches without notes.** She prepares extensively the night before but does not bring paper into the room. Her instructional manner is Socratic, patient, and noticeably warmer than her council manner. Students of every cohort describe her the same way across forty years: *she remembered things I said two weeks ago, she asked me about my sister, she waited for me to finish.* The waiting is the most striking habit. She allows silences in conversation that most people cannot tolerate. Surveillance audio of her classes shows mean pause-after-student-question durations of 4–7 seconds before she responds. Most instructors respond in under 1.5.

**She does not eat lunch with colleagues.** This is consistent across every documented era and is one of the most reliable behavioral markers in the file. She takes lunch alone, almost always outdoors when weather permits, usually walking with food in hand rather than seated. The midday solitary interval appears to be a required decompression. Attempts by well-meaning colleagues to recruit her into a lunchtime social pattern have been deflected, gently, for decades. She will accept a dinner invitation. She will not accept a lunch invitation. The pattern is invariant.

**In council settings she speaks late and briefly.** Across the Quiet Council period, transcripts show she contributed to roughly 18–22% of verbal exchanges by word count, well below her peers, but her interventions correlated very highly with subsequent decisions reversing direction. She lets the room run, listens, then speaks once with a question rather than an assertion. She uses no oratorical flourish. She does not raise her voice. She has been observed, in heated meetings, to *lower* hers — to the point that other speakers stop talking because they cannot hear her. This is a deliberate technique. It is the only aggressive interpersonal move she reliably deploys.

---

## 6. THE PRACTICE INTERVAL

Between the work day and the evening, Subject takes between forty-five and ninety minutes for what she calls "practice" and what observers should categorize as *daily containment maintenance*. This is non-negotiable. She has missed it on perhaps fewer than thirty occasions in her adult life and the pattern of those missed days correlates almost perfectly with subsequent Phoenix-state instabilities.

The practice has three phases:

- **Telekinetic fine-motor work.** She manipulates small objects — sand, water droplets, the leaves of a single plant, occasionally writing implements — at the edge of her perceptual precision. This is *down-regulation* training: keeping the smallest movements available means keeping the largest in check. Surveillance would show her sitting cross-legged on the floor of whatever space she has designated, eyes half-closed, motionless except for the slowest possible movement of (e.g.) a single droplet of water tracing a figure-eight in the air a meter from her face. This phase typically takes twenty to thirty minutes.
- **Telepathic perimeter and shield work.** She erects, dismantles, and re-erects her own mental shields in sequence, varying the architecture each session. This is the equivalent of a martial artist running forms. She does this with eyes closed and is unresponsive to verbal stimuli during it. Partners have learned not to interrupt; the one or two times Summers has had to break in for emergency reasons, she has come out of it with a marked headache and visible irritation — among the only contexts in which she expresses irritation at him openly.
- **Phoenix communion / sequestering.** This is the phase she will not discuss with anyone, including her partners. She enters a brief meditative state — five to fifteen minutes — in which, by inference, she communicates with or compartmentalizes the residual Phoenix presence. She emerges from it visibly different than she emerged from the prior two phases: slightly flushed, pupils slightly dilated, with a brief window (perhaps two minutes) during which her voice is half a register lower and her phrasing more elliptical. Then she returns to baseline. **This is the most diagnostically important fifteen minutes of her day.** No one has ever observed it in detail. She does it behind a closed door.

She showers immediately after. Always.

---

## 7. EVENING — COMMUNAL MEAL AND PROXIMITY

The evening meal is the most consistently social interval of her day and the one in which she most resembles a person without a clinical history. She cooks, often, and well; she enjoys feeding people; she keeps the wine pour modest (she drinks rarely and lightly, never more than two glasses, often none — see Section 2 of the analytical workup); she laughs more easily here than at any other time. Surveillance audio from dinners across the years catches her, repeatedly, telling the same handful of stories — childhood Annandale anecdotes, an early X-Men mission that went absurdly wrong, a thing one of her students once said — and laughing at them as if hearing them for the first time. The repetition is itself comforting to her; the stories are touchstones.

After the meal, she keeps physical proximity to her partners without necessarily speaking. She reads on the couch with her feet under Summers's leg. She lets Frost paint her nails (a Treehouse-era development that surveillance would have flagged as out-of-character for both women and that is, in fact, one of the more telling intimacy-data points in the file). She does not watch much screen-based entertainment; when she does, it is documentary or naturalist programming, never crime drama, never anything featuring telepathic plot elements.

She makes a single phone call or its equivalent most evenings — to Rachel, when Rachel is in this reality; to Nathan when he can be reached; less often to her sister Sara's surviving family. The calls are short. She does not perform availability; she checks in, registers the voice, signs off. The act of hearing the living voice of a person she loves is the evening equivalent of the morning perimeter sweep.

---

## 8. LATE NIGHT — THE READING INTERVAL

Between 22:00 and 00:30 — sometimes later — she reads alone. This is the longest sustained solitary interval of her day. She reads omnivorously: poetry (Rilke, Oliver, Glück across the eras she has lived through; the Rilke is constant), theology and comparative religion (notably Buddhist source texts and the Christian mystics — Julian of Norwich is a documented favorite), clinical psychology (she keeps current on the trauma literature, which she would not describe as autobiographical but which observably is), and fiction of a particular kind — long, slow, character-interior novels, almost never plot-driven. She is the kind of reader who finishes a book, sits with it for several minutes, and then immediately begins it again from the start. She has done this with a small canon of perhaps a dozen books, recurring across decades.

She journals. Not daily, not in a structured way, but several times a week, in physical notebooks, in a small precise hand. The notebooks are kept somewhere none of her partners have ever seen. Subject has, over forty years, generated an unknown but substantial volume of private written material that no one has read. This is the single largest data gap in the file and probably the most significant.

She reinforces her shields once more before sleep, more elaborately than the morning version — a full perimeter, layered. She kisses her partners. She sleeps on her left side, facing the door.

---

## 9. THE SMALL HABITS — TICS, TELLS, AND GROUND-TRUTH MARKERS

Things a long surveillance file would catalog and that, taken together, are her behavioral fingerprint:

- **The hair gesture.** When thinking she pulls a strand of hair forward from behind her ear and twists it once around her finger before letting it fall back. Frequency increases with cognitive load. Disappears entirely during dissociative episodes — *its absence is a warning sign*.
- **The two-finger temple touch.** Right hand, index and middle finger, briefly to her right temple. This is a telepathy-regulation gesture; she does it when she is closing a channel she had opened. Most people read it as a headache tell. It is not.
- **The breath-before-speaking pause.** Even in trivial conversation, she takes a small breath before she begins to speak. Always. The breath is the gate.
- **Color avoidance.** She does not wear pure red in daily life. Operational uniforms aside, her wardrobe trends to deep greens, earth tones, oxblood, cream, slate, and black. Pure saturated red is absent. This is unremarked-upon and rigorous.
- **Door behavior.** She closes doors she has passed through. She does not leave doors open behind her. In open-plan spaces she sits with her back to a wall.
- **The single-syllable laugh.** When genuinely amused, she produces a quiet, single-syllable laugh — a "huh" — before the actual laugh follows. Intimates recognize it as the marker of real amusement versus social laughter, which is fuller and quicker and less reliable.
- **Plant-touching.** Already noted in the morning sequence; she does it throughout the day, often unconsciously, when passing any growing thing.
- **Eye-contact duration.** Unusually long with intimates (3–6 seconds), unusually brief with strangers (under 1 second), with a distinct *deliberate look-away* — she breaks the gaze rather than letting it dissolve, which most strangers experience as warmth rather than as the boundary it actually is.
- **The Annie pause.** Once every several weeks, surveillance would catch her stopping mid-activity — mid-sentence, mid-step, mid-pour — and going briefly still for two or three seconds with no observable trigger. Then she resumes. This is, by all available inference, an intrusive recollection. She does not announce it. She does not appear to register that she has stopped. The people closest to her have learned to wait through it without comment.

---

## 10. THE WEEKLY AND MONTHLY RHYTHMS

**Weekly:** She takes one full day, almost always the equivalent of Sunday, on which she conducts no scheduled work and accepts no obligations. The Sabbath observance is not religious in any denominational sense and she does not call it that, but its structure is recognizably one. She cooks more elaborately. She is in the garden if there is a garden. She is in physical contact with her partners more than usual. She does not check news. She does not take meetings.

**Monthly:** Once a month, on a date she does not telegraph but that an attentive surveillance log would identify as falling near the new moon, she takes several hours entirely alone, away from the residence, often in wilderness if it is accessible. She returns calm. She does not explain. This appears to be an extended version of the Phoenix communion phase of her daily practice — a longer reckoning with the part of herself she keeps in a closed room.

**Annually:** Two dates in her year are observably weighted. One is in early spring and corresponds, by archival reconstruction, to the anniversary of Annie Richardson's death. The other is in summer and corresponds to one of her own deaths — she has not specified which, and the candidates are several. On both, she is quieter than usual, eats less, reads more, does not teach if she can avoid it, and asks her partners — without ceremony — to stay close. They do.

---

## 11. WHAT A WEEK OF SURVEILLANCE WOULD ACTUALLY YIELD

A surveillance team running a full week on Subject and reporting at the end of it would file, if they were honest, the following précis:

*Subject lives a quiet, highly ordered life of teaching, partnered domesticity, governance work, and disciplined personal practice. Affect is consistently warm, modulated, and contained. No substance use. No financial irregularities. No undisclosed contacts. No deceptive behaviors observed. Subject appears to be one of the most stable individuals in her cohort.*

That report would be wrong in the way that matters.

What the surveillance would have actually documented, if the analyst knew what to look for, is a person running an unbroken forty-year containment protocol of formidable sophistication: every partition of her day a small lock on a much larger door, every ritual a check on a system that has failed catastrophically before and that she does not believe can be allowed to fail again. The stability is real. It is also *manufactured, hourly, by her*. The day she stops performing the rituals is the day to watch.

The morning perimeter sweep. The east-facing window. The pre-poured water glass. The single droplet tracing a figure-eight in the air. The closed door for fifteen minutes a day. The notebooks no one has read.

These are not the habits of a settled person. They are the habits of a person who has built, out of the materials of an ordinary domestic life, a continuously operating cathedral of self-regulation — and who walks through it, every day, with the grace of someone who has long since stopped noticing she is doing it.

— END SECTION —


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*Subject: Jean Grey-Summers. Section scope: the bonds of blood, of origin, and of the dead — the human armature beneath the cosmic biography. These are the relationships from which every later attachment is a derivation, a repetition, or a repair attempt.*

---

## 1. ELAINE GREY (mother) — *the lost calm*

**History.** Elaine Grey, née Bogart, professor's wife and homemaker of the Annandale-on-Hudson household, is the first attuned presence in the subject's life and — critically — the one adult in the entire dossier who knew Jean *before the mutation foregrounded itself*. The household is reconstructable in considerable detail from canon and from the texture of Jean's later domestic preferences: a brick faculty home on a tree-lined street, books in every room, classical music on Sundays, Elaine cooking from a small rotation of recipes that recur in Jean's adult kitchen (a vegetable-heavy minestrone; a particular almond cake brought out for birthdays). Elaine is the mother who held the catatonic ten-year-old after Annie Richardson died and did not, by any account, flinch from her.

**Dynamics.** Elaine's parenting style is reconstructable as warm-attuned-pragmatic, with a streak of the practical New England intellectual who *organizes* care rather than performing it. She is the one who insisted, against John's initial scholar's preference to wait-and-see, that the silent child be taken to specialists; she is the one who, on Xavier's offer of help, asked the harder questions (canon shows Elaine, not John, as the more skeptical interrogator of Xavier in flashback). The granular tell here is significant: Jean's adult pattern of *seeking out competent help and then doubting it* is Elaine's pattern, not John's.

**Evolution.** From early childhood to age ten: ordinary close mother-daughter bond, with the standard middle-child negotiations against an older sister's territoriality. From ten to mid-teens: Elaine is the stable container while Jean is being psychiatrically and then psionically managed by external authorities; she is, behaviorally, the one Jean returns *home to* from Xavier's, the one who notices weight, sleep, mood. From mid-teens onward, distance accumulates structurally — Westchester is two hours from Annandale but might as well be a different planet — and the relationship migrates to weekly phone calls, school-holiday visits, and a sustained, slightly formal correspondence (Elaine writes letters by hand into the 1990s, which Jean keeps).

**Trust / safety.** High and uncomplicated, with one specific exception: Jean does not, ever, tell Elaine the full content of any Phoenix episode. She tells Scott. She tells Xavier (some of it). She tells Storm. She does not tell her mother. This is not estrangement; it is curation — the longest-running and most consistent piece of *protective withholding* in the subject's record. Elaine reads about the Dark Phoenix events in the newspaper.

**Failure mode.** Death at the hands of Shi'ar-affiliated agents (the Phalanx/Shi'ar Death Commandos arc, executed in canon as part of the cycle of retributions for Phoenix-related crimes). Elaine is murdered in the Annandale house, in the kitchen Jean grew up in, for the offense of having borne Jean Grey. This event — *her mother killed in punishment for what she herself did in a dissociated state she does not fully remember* — is the single most clinically corrosive datum in the entire family file. It activates simultaneously: survivor guilt for a real death; retroactive guilt for Phoenix acts; the foundational Annie-pattern (intimacy with me kills); and a permanent verification of the childhood-installed lesson that her mind is dangerous to those nearest her.

**Leverage.** Elaine is dead, and therefore is not leverage in the operational sense. But the *idea* of Elaine — the kitchen, the almond cake, the unread letters in a box in the Treehouse — is the single most reliable route to baseline-Jean grief, the kind that bypasses the over-control. An operator wishing to crack the composure does not invoke the Phoenix; they invoke a recipe.

---

## 2. JOHN GREY (father) — *the absent witness*

**History.** Dr. John Grey, professor of history at Bard College (in some tellings, classics; the canon wobbles, the function is identical), is the parent Jean intellectually resembles and emotionally diverges from. Tall, thin, bookish, soft-spoken, the kind of academic father who is *present in the house and absent in the room* — grading at the dining table while children move around him. Jean inherits from him: the synthetic-integrative cognitive style, the taste for long reading, the slightly formal vocabulary that surfaces under stress, the habit of standing slightly apart in a crowd.

**Dynamics.** John's parenting register is *respectful* — he speaks to his daughters as small adults from the time they can speak — which is a gift to a precocious child and a liability to a traumatized one. When Annie dies, John's response is to *think about it carefully*, which produces an interval (weeks, per canonical flashback) in which the catatonic child is reasoned with rather than held. Elaine breaks the impasse. This is the template for every later dynamic with John: he loves accurately and acts slowly, and Jean has learned not to wait for him in a crisis.

**Evolution.** Adolescence through young adulthood: a courteous, slightly distant warmth, mediated through books exchanged by mail (he sends her novels; she returns them annotated). Through the Phoenix era and after: a *deepening* — John, alone of the family, attempts to read the public record about his daughter and form his own view, which she finds touching and unbearable in roughly equal measure. He never, in any panel, asks her *what it was like to be Phoenix*. She never volunteers. The silence is mutual and is mistaken on both sides for respect.

**Trust / safety.** Trust: complete. Safety: complicated. Jean is safe from John in the sense that he will never harm her; she is not safe with him in the sense that she has never been able to bring her actual interior to him without watching him recoil into thought. The Annie-era pattern reproduces.

**Failure mode.** Killed alongside Elaine in the Annandale house. The granular detail to register is that John's death is, in canon, depicted as *protective* — he is killed trying to interpose, an old man with no powers, against opponents he cannot affect. This matters psychologically because it inverts the lifelong pattern: for one moment, John acts before he thinks, on Jean's behalf, and dies of it. Jean inherits the image and cannot put it down.

**Leverage.** A father's annotated copy of a book, returned to her after his death, will produce a longer collapse than a threat. The operational point: the Grey parents are not used as leverage by sophisticated operators because the leverage *takes too long to recover from* — it puts the asset out of commission for days, not minutes.

---

## 3. SARA GREY-BAILEY (older sister) — *the ordinary one*

**History.** Sara Grey, two to four years Jean's senior depending on the telling, is the non-mutant sibling, the one who got the unremarkable life: married Paul Bailey, two children (Joey and Gailyn), suburban household, a job, a normal middle-class American shape. She is the control case in the Grey family experiment and therefore, structurally, the most important sibling relationship in the subject's psychology — the constant reminder of the life Jean did not get to have and, in another register, the life she would not have chosen even if offered.

**Dynamics.** Childhood: standard older-sister territoriality complicated, after the mutation manifests, by Sara's *fear* of her sister. Canon is explicit: Sara was frightened of Jean as a child after the Annie event and again after the powers became visible, and that fear, though it softened, never fully resolved. Jean's behavioral response was — predictably — to make herself smaller around Sara, to suppress and to perform normalcy on visits. Sara's adult re-evaluation is genuine and warm: she loves her sister, defends her in public, names a daughter as a kind of bridge to her, and is the family member who *visits* the X-Mansion when others won't.

**Evolution.** The arc is reconciliation-deepening-loss. The two sisters reach, by Jean's late twenties, a real adult friendship, organized around the niece and nephew and around the shared work of being the Grey daughters in a family becoming famous for the wrong reasons. Sara is the only person in Jean's life who teases her about her hair, her clothes, her seriousness — the only relationship in the record that contains *sibling levity*.

**Trust / safety.** Trust: high and earned twice over. Safety: high, with a specific asymmetry — Sara has been afraid of Jean and they both know it, which means Jean monitors her own affect around Sara in a way she does not around Scott or Storm. The monitoring is loving, not resentful, but it is monitoring.

**Failure mode.** Murdered, with her children, in the same Shi'ar Death Commandos sweep that took the parents. Sara's children — Jean's niece and nephew, the only family children she ever held as an aunt — die in the same operation. The compounded loss is what no profile can adequately weight: Jean did not merely lose her sister; she lost the *only ordinary thread* she had to a non-mutant life and the only children in her direct lineage whom she had watched grow from infancy.

**Leverage.** Posthumous and total. References to Joey and Gailyn — the niece and nephew — bypass every defense the subject has built. Sophisticated handlers would not deploy this; it produces grief, not compliance.

---

## 4. ANNIE RICHARDSON (childhood best friend, deceased) — *the wound that became a structure*

**History.** Annie Richardson, age approximately ten, neighbor and best friend, struck by a car in front of the Grey house in Annandale. Jean ran to her, held her, and — in the act of holding — experienced the involuntary first manifestation of her telepathy: she was inside Annie's mind when Annie died, and felt the dying as if it were her own. This event is the origin of everything in the dossier. It is the foundational trauma; it is the first telepathic contact; it is the first lesson about the danger of intimacy; it is the first time an adult intervened in her mind to make her able to bear it.

**Dynamics (pre-death).** Reconstructable from the texture of Jean's later loyalties: Annie was, by every implication, the *first chosen intimate* outside the family — the friend who came over after school, the friend whose bedroom Jean knew as well as her own, the friend with whom she had whatever the ten-year-old version of merger is. The behavioral evidence is that Jean has, ever since, oriented her closest friendships in pairs of *one* — a single best friend at a time, deeply held: in adolescence, Misty Knight on the periphery; in adulthood, Storm centrally and for decades.

**Evolution after death.** Annie does not evolve; Jean evolves around Annie. The first phase is catatonic withdrawal (weeks to months), mutism, refusal of food, the recognizable acute pediatric dissociative response. The second phase is the Xavier intervention, after which Annie becomes *a sealed compartment* — Jean is permitted, by the psionic wall, to remember Annie without re-experiencing the death-merger every time. The third phase, unfolding over decades, is the slow recognition (which Jean reaches in the Morrison era and again in Krakoa) that *Annie is the template* — every act of bodily self-sacrifice on behalf of another is a re-staging, every choice to take the seat in the shuttle, every choice to absorb the energy meant for someone else.

**Trust / safety.** N/A in operational terms. In psychological terms: Annie is the only relationship in the file that retains an *uncomplicated* valence — she was loved, she died, she did nothing wrong, she is missed. Every other death in the file is contaminated by guilt or by the suspicion of having caused it. Annie is *clean grief*, and as such functions almost as a religious object — the still point against which all the rest of the cosmology is measured.

**Failure mode.** Already failed. The relationship is the failure. The structural lesson — *to be close to me is to die in my head* — has organized forty years of behavior and cannot be unlearned by being told it is untrue.

**Leverage.** Mention of Annie's name, by any voice not Jean's own, is treated by the subject as a near-sacred intrusion and produces immediate, controlled withdrawal — not collapse. The defense around Annie is, uniquely, *intact*. It has had longer to set than any other defense in the system. An operator using Annie as a lever produces silence, not compliance; the subject simply leaves the room. This is the only family-origin lever in the file that *does not work*, and that fact is itself diagnostic — it is the wound she has, through forty years of unwilling practice, learned to carry without flinching.

---

## 5. CHARLES XAVIER (functional parent / first surgeon of her mind) — *the unconsenting bond*

**History.** Charles Xavier enters the household when Jean is approximately eleven, on referral, presented to the Grey parents as a specialist in childhood psychiatric conditions with a particular interest in cases like their daughter's. Within his first sustained contact with the child, he performs — without informed consent from a minor patient and with consent from parents who could not possibly have understood what was being consented to — a psionic intervention that walls off her telepathy and leaves only telekinesis active. This is the second formative event of the dossier and, in clinical terms, the iatrogenic ground on which everything subsequent grows.

**Dynamics.** Xavier is, simultaneously and incompatibly: rescuer (he ended the catatonia), surrogate father (she lives in his house through adolescence and young adulthood), teacher, employer, commanding officer, and the man who has been inside her head without her permission. Jean's adult relationship to him is *unfailingly correct* — she addresses him as Professor for decades into adulthood, defers to him in council, defends him in public — and *structurally compromised at the root*. The compromise rarely surfaces as overt anger; it surfaces as a particular flatness in her voice when she speaks of him, as the avoidance of unstructured time alone with him, and, in the Onslaught aftermath, as the first observable *cold* moments she has ever displayed toward any attachment figure.

**Evolution.** Adolescence: idealization, gratitude, daughterly attachment. Twenties: complicated loyalty during the original X-Men era, sustained by the obvious good he was doing and undermined, periodically, by the famous internal monologue (Xavier acknowledging to himself an attraction to his student) — material Jean did not consciously read but, given her telepathy and his porousness, almost certainly registered preconsciously. Phoenix era: he is the one who attempts to install fresh walls during the Dark Phoenix decompensation, with limited success; the lifelong pattern of him reaching in to "fix" her recurs at the worst possible moment. Onslaught era: definitive confirmation that her formative therapist had been carrying his own large unprocessed shadow, which had been *adjacent to her mind* for her entire developmental period. Krakoa era: a careful, professional distance, Quiet Council collegiality, the warmth of long association without the daughterly deference. She has, by this stage, finished with him as a parental object — quietly, without rupture, without ever naming it.

**Trust / safety.** Trust: instrumental, high. Safety: low at the structural level she does not articulate. She trusts him to be Xavier; she does not trust him not to reach in.

**Failure mode.** The single most consequential failure in the entire dossier. The walls he installed were the substrate Mastermind used to construct the Black Queen identity. Every subsequent dissociative episode runs partly along grooves he cut. He never apologized in terms commensurate with the injury; she never asked him to.

**Leverage.** Operationally, Xavier himself is not a lever — the relationship is too defended. The *pattern* he installed is the lever, deployed by every later operator who has tried to reach into her mind. The vulnerability is not "Xavier" as a person; it is the architecture he left behind.

---

## 6. NATHAN CHRISTOPHER CHARLES SUMMERS / CABLE (son, biological-by-proxy, time-displaced) — *the child she did not raise*

**History.** Nathan is the biological son of Scott Summers and Madelyne Pryor (Jean's clone), infected with the techno-organic virus by Apocalypse, sent two thousand years into the future to be cured, raised there to adulthood, and returned to the present as a man older than his parents. Jean's biological relationship to him is by way of Madelyne's genome, which is her genome; her *experienced* relationship to him is as the stepmother / second mother who arrives after the fact of his entire life.

**Dynamics.** The dynamic is one of the strangest in the file and is handled by Jean with a grace that does not survive close inspection without revealing how much it costs her. She meets her son when he is older than she is, scarred, militarized, time-broken, and carrying the imprint of a war she will never see. She loves him on contact — the canon is unambiguous on this — and never, in the record, performs the role of mother in a way that would embarrass him or her. She mothers him by being *available* and *not insisting*, which is the only registration of mothering a man like Cable can tolerate.

**Evolution.** From first contact through the Askani arc, in which Jean and Scott are *temporally* projected into the future and live as Redd and Slym, raising the child Nathan for approximately a decade in a body and life not their own. This is, behaviorally and clinically, the *only sustained experience of parenting an actual child* in Jean's recorded life — twelve years in a borrowed life, in a future, of a son who is also a grown man in her present. The integration of these memories is one of the great quiet feats of her psychology. She speaks of the Askani years rarely; she carries them constantly.

**Trust / safety.** Trust: deep, mutual, sober. Safety: high; Cable is one of the few people in the file who can be in Jean's presence in a Phoenix-adjacent state and remain operationally calm, partly by virtue of his own telepathy and partly by virtue of having spent a childhood with her in the Askani timeline.

**Failure mode.** Failure modes are not interpersonal here — they are temporal and ontological. The relationship has been *good*; the loss is structural. She did not get to raise her son in her own life. The Askani memories are real, and are also not the same as having done it here.

**Leverage.** Threat to Cable destabilizes Jean, but Cable is famously difficult to threaten; the lever is theoretical more than operational. The more usable lever is the *Askani memory itself* — invocations of Redd, of the child Nathan, of the years in the future — which produces in Jean a softness that is otherwise quite rare in her professional register.

---

## 7. RACHEL SUMMERS / ANNE / PRESTIGE (daughter from a divergent timeline) — *the child of the worst future*

**History.** Rachel is the daughter Jean and Scott would have had in a timeline (Days of Future Past / the Mutant Hound future) that did not occur in the prime continuity, displaced into the present, where she meets her mother who has not borne her. Rachel grew up hunted, conscripted as a Hound, used as a psychic bloodhound to track and kill her own kind; she arrived in the present already brutalized, already a Phoenix host in her own right, already carrying her mother's signature on her own power.

**Dynamics.** The bond is immediate and asymmetric. Rachel needs her mother with the intensity of a woman who has never had one and has spent years imagining the version she was denied. Jean meets a daughter she did not conceive, whose face she recognizes as her own, who carries her power, who is asking for the mothering of a child and is presenting as a damaged adult. Jean's response — across decades of canon — is to extend the mothering without ever overcorrecting the asymmetry: she does not pretend the timeline is hers, she does not perform a maternity she did not earn, and she does not withhold the love Rachel needs. This is delicate work and Jean does it well.

**Evolution.** Early phase: cautious mutual recognition, Phoenix-to-Phoenix legibility, Rachel's overwhelming need handled with restraint. Middle phase: genuine mother-daughter operational partnership in X-Factor and later teams; Rachel as the daughter Jean both has and does not have. Krakoa era: a maturing peer-adjacency, Rachel as an adult with her own life, the mothering register softening into something closer to mentorship-with-love.

**Trust / safety.** Trust: deep and tested. Safety: layered — both are Phoenix hosts, both know what the other could do, both have learned not to be afraid of each other.

**Failure mode.** The structural failure is that Rachel is, in part, evidence that Jean's worst possible future already happened *somewhere*, and that her daughter lived in it. Jean cannot repair the timeline Rachel came from. The accommodation is permanent.

**Leverage.** Rachel in danger collapses Jean's composure on a timescale of seconds. This is the most operationally relevant family lever in the active file — Cable can defend himself, the Grey parents are dead, Annie is sacred and defended — Rachel is alive, present, vulnerable in the way only an Omega-but-not-quite-Mom telepath can be vulnerable, and Jean's mothering instinct toward her is unguarded.

---

## 8. NATE GREY / X-MAN (the son who is not her son) — *the boy who calls her mother*

**History.** Nate Grey is the Age of Apocalypse counterpart of Cable, gestated from Scott and Jean's combined genetic material in Sinister's lab in an alternate reality, displaced into the prime timeline, and possessed of an Omega-level psionic capacity that approaches Phoenix-tier. He addresses Jean, periodically, as *mother*; she is, periodically, willing to accept the address.

**Dynamics.** The relationship is the *least resolved* of the parental-adjacent bonds. Jean's biological relationship to Nate is genuine in a sense she did not consent to; her experienced relationship to him is intermittent, often crisis-driven, complicated by Nate's own instability and by his repeated approaches to her in states of psionic distress. She mothers him conditionally and incompletely, and is honest with herself about the limit.

**Trust / safety.** Trust: moderate, qualified. Safety: variable — Nate's instability has, at times, made him dangerous to the people around him, including her.

**Failure mode.** Nate, more than any other figure in the family file, embodies the unresolved problem of Jean's *unconsented reproductive history* — children made from her genome by external actors, in laboratories and in futures, returning to her as adults asking for things she did not agree to provide. Her management of this is competent and grieved.

**Leverage.** Nate is not a clean lever — he is too unstable to be used reliably — but the *category* he represents (children of her body she did not bear) is a standing wound that any sufficiently informed operator can press.

---

## 9. MADELYNE PRYOR (clone / "sister" / absorbed self, deceased and recurring) — *the disowned twin*

**History.** Madelyne is Jean's genetic duplicate, manufactured by Sinister as a back-up vessel and as bait for Scott, who married her, fathered a child with her, and abandoned her when the original Jean returned. Madelyne, brutalized by the


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*Filed under Subject 0617-GREY-J. Cross-reference Relationships I (Family of Origin & Romantic) and Relationships III (Adversaries & Ambiguous Bonds). The persons mapped here are those whose presence in the Subject's life is, on balance, regulating rather than destabilizing — though the file will not pretend the distinction is clean. The Subject's relational topology is dense, recursive, and includes several persons who have at different epochs occupied incompatible categories. Each entry is constructed as a longitudinal dossier: origin of contact, dynamic baseline, observed evolution across decades, the trust-and-safety topography between them, the predictable failure mode, and the leverage either party holds (witting or unwitting) over the other.*

---

## 1. CHARLES XAVIER — Mentor, Surrogate Father, Founding Iatrogenic Agent

**Origin of contact.** Brought to the Subject's family by her parents at approximately age ten, in the months following the Annie Richardson event, when the Subject was mute or near-mute, sleeping poorly, and exhibiting the behavioral signature of a child whose nervous system had not closed the loop on a death-merger. Xavier presented as a credentialed academic — a genetics researcher with psychiatric training — and was permitted, by educated parents in genuine extremis, to do something that no licensed practitioner could have done legally: he reached into the child's mind and altered it.

**Dynamic baseline.** From this first contact forward, Xavier occupies a structurally compromised role in the Subject's life. He is simultaneously: (a) the man who quieted the unbearable, for which she is permanently grateful; (b) the man who decided, without her informed consent and without the comprehension capacity of a ten-year-old, which of her faculties she would have access to and on what schedule; (c) the surrogate father who taught her, trained her, named her (Marvel Girl), and modeled the use of telepathy itself. Every subsequent relationship she has with a powerful older man, with a teacher, with an authority who claims to "see" her, runs over the substrate this bond laid down.

**Evolution.** Through adolescence and the early X-Men years she is the *good daughter* of the school — diligent, deferential, the one who internalizes Xavier's value system most completely. Through the Phoenix and Dark Phoenix years she begins, without ever quite saying so, to notice. The walls he installed are the structural weakness Mastermind exploits; she registers this on the cognitive level even as she does not, in that era, permit herself to name it as fault. Through the Onslaught arc — the externalization of Xavier's own dissociated shadow material as a world-ending entity — the symmetry becomes inescapable: *her therapist was symptomatic*. By the post-Morrison and Krakoan eras she relates to him with the mature, slightly cool clarity of an adult child who has done the work the parent never did. She loves him; she does not trust his judgment about minds.

**Trust / safety topography.** Asymmetric and degraded. He has had inside her in a way no one else in her life has. She has never had inside him at any comparable depth, and on the occasions she has glimpsed his architecture (Onslaught, Danger, the Shi'ar prosecution, the secret-keeping around Moira), she has found rooms she was not shown. The safety she feels with him is largely the safety of a known animal: she can predict him.

**Failure mode.** Xavier overrides her consent in the name of a larger plan she would, if asked, have agreed to anyway — and the overriding, not the plan, does the damage. This has happened at least once at every developmental stage of her life and there is no evidence he has learned not to do it.

**Leverage.** He retains, at the level of nervous system, the parental authority of the person who first made the noise stop. She retains, at the level of the cosmos, every reason and capacity to undo him; she has never used it and her not-using it is the moral architecture of the relationship.

---

## 2. ORORO MUNROE / STORM — The Sister of Record

**Origin of contact.** Storm arrives with the second team (Giant-Size X-Men #1, 1975) into a house the Subject had effectively left; their early overlap is brief but immediate. Two women of comparable power and dissimilar background, in a cohort otherwise dominated by men, find each other quickly.

**Dynamic baseline.** This is the Subject's most *lateral* significant relationship — neither caretaking-down nor deferring-up, but eye-to-eye. Storm is one of the few persons in the Subject's life who is not, on net, a project for her: she does not need to be managed, contained, mentored, or held together. She has her own discipline of self, her own theology of restraint, her own history of catastrophic power held under conscious rein (claustrophobia, godhood in Kenya, the loss of her powers in the 80s). The two women recognize each other.

**Evolution.** Through the late 1970s the friendship is companionable and quiet — significant for what it does *not* require. After the Subject's first death, Storm grieves her in a register the male X-Men cannot match; the funeral material in Uncanny is the most affectively honest depiction of mourning the Subject ever receives. Post-resurrection, the bond resumes without renegotiation, which is itself rare in the Subject's record. Through the Krakoan era they sit on adjacent organs of governance (Storm on the Quiet Council and as a Regent; the Subject on the Council), and the file logs repeated instances of them coordinating before formal sessions in a register that reads as old marriage.

**Trust / safety.** The highest in the Subject's peer cohort. Storm is one of perhaps three persons in the world to whom the Subject will admit, without performance of stoicism, that she is tired.

**Failure mode.** Mutual courtesy. Each is so attentive to the other's autonomy that genuine confrontation between them is rare; when one is heading for catastrophe, the other tends to grant her the space to choose it. Neither has ever, on record, said the hard thing to the other in time.

**Leverage.** None used. Each could, on the weather and on the mind respectively, end the other. The relationship is conducted in the full mutual awareness of that fact and the deliberate, decade-long refusal to weaponize it.

---

## 3. HENRY "HANK" McCOY / BEAST — The Brother, the Witness, the Liability

**Origin of contact.** Founding team. Hank is one of the four young men in the Subject's first cohort and the one who, almost from the start, declines the romantic queue. He is her *friend* in the specific, rare sense — the male peer with whom her bond is not eroticized.

**Dynamic baseline.** Intellectual companionship; shared humor of a dry, allusive sort; mutual respect for cognition. He is the team member to whom she would, in the early years, take a question of fact rather than a question of feeling. He is also, across decades, the most attentive observer of her somatic and neurological state — the one most likely to notice, in passing, that her resting heart rate is elevated or that her telekinetic field has acquired a new harmonic.

**Evolution.** Stable through the Silver and Bronze Age. Strained, then deeply compromised, in the X-Force / Krakoan era as Hank's behavior shifts toward authoritarian, ethically corrupted, increasingly grotesque conduct (the X-Force black-ops, the Krakoan-era atrocities, the eventual estrangement from his own moral architecture). The Subject is on record across multiple incidents as having noticed, named, and failed to interdict; she has, by the late Krakoan era, lost the friend in any meaningful operational sense while continuing to remember him.

**Trust / safety.** Historically very high; presently provisional and grief-tinged. She would not, today, leave a child of hers in his care.

**Failure mode.** She catalogues the deterioration with clinical precision and continues to behave socially as if the older Hank is recoverable. The pattern is consistent with her broader tendency to grant intimates the benefit of an integration she herself has had to do.

**Leverage.** He knows her vitals. She knows his decay. Neither piece of information has been used.

---

## 4. KURT WAGNER / NIGHTCRAWLER — The Confessor

**Origin of contact.** Giant-Size #1 cohort; she meets him after her first transformation into Phoenix. He is one of the few X-Men whose initial relationship to her is to *Phoenix-Jean* rather than to *Marvel-Girl-Jean*.

**Dynamic baseline.** Kurt is the Subject's closest approach to a non-romantic confessor. His theology is real, his courtesy is structural, and he does not flinch from the demonic-presenting or the cosmically large. The Subject — who has been called demon, goddess, and worse, often accurately — finds in him a man who will hold the metaphysics seriously and the person tenderly at the same time.

**Evolution.** Through the late 70s their bond is warm but not central. Across the Excalibur years (Kurt abroad) it goes dormant. Through the 2000s and into Krakoa it re-emerges; his Spark / Mercy-era theological work, and her own deep history with souls and the White Hot Room, give them shared technical vocabulary almost no one else has. He is one of three people to whom she has spoken plainly about what happens to her between deaths.

**Trust / safety.** Very high. The specific safety is that he will neither minimize the cosmic content of her experience nor instrumentalize it.

**Failure mode.** He will absolve her. The Subject does not, in fact, need more absolution; she needs to be *contradicted* about her culpability for the D'Bari and adjacent events, and Kurt's pastoral instinct is to comfort.

**Leverage.** None. The relationship is one of the few in her file with no observed extraction in either direction.

---

## 5. LOGAN / WOLVERINE — Loved, Dangerous, Held at Distance

**Origin of contact.** Giant-Size #1. He imprints on her with the speed and totality characteristic of him and she registers it within the first weeks. From that point forward, the unconsummated romantic charge between them is one of the foundational facts of her cohort's social field.

**Dynamic baseline.** *He is in love with her; she loves him; she will not have him.* This sentence, in some form, governs forty years of their interaction. She does not pretend the charge does not exist (cf. Morrison-era explicit telepathic acknowledgment); she also will not, except in alternate timelines and end-of-the-world scenarios, act on it. Operationally he functions as a brother-in-arms whose attention she trusts unconditionally and whose body she keeps on the other side of a precise, never-discussed line.

**Evolution.** The geometry holds with remarkable stability across decades. He is at her funerals. He is present at the Dark Phoenix climax on the Moon and is one of the very few persons whose violence she would, if it came to that, accept as containment. In several apocalyptic alternates he is the man she chose; she carries the memory of those choices in her cellular record after each resurrection without ever, in the prime timeline, allowing it to redirect her.

**Trust / safety.** Total within the relationship's defined geometry; weaponizable if the geometry is violated. He has been, on at least three separate cosmic occasions, the man instructed in advance to kill her if containment failed. He has performed the function.

**Failure mode.** The arrangement requires the Subject to manage his pain across decades, which she does competently and at quiet cost. It also requires Scott to tolerate him at the breakfast table, which Scott does with diminishing grace.

**Leverage.** She could, with a sentence, change the configuration of his life; she has never spoken the sentence. He could, with a claw, end her body; he has, in extremity, done so. The mutual restraint is the relationship.

---

## 6. EMMA FROST — Rival, Co-Wife, Mirror, Working Partner

*Cross-filed with Relationships I; entered here because the contemporary functional bond is collegial and chosen.*

**Origin of contact.** Adversarial — Hellfire Club, White Queen versus the X-Men, with explicit telepathic combat between the two women that is, in retrospect, the first time the Subject met another woman of comparable psionic register who *did not* defer to her.

**Dynamic baseline.** The relationship moves, across thirty years of publication time, from antagonist to rival to interloper to co-parent of the same marriage to colleague to something for which there is no adequate English word. The Subject *forced* the integration in the dying telepathic act of the Morrison run — pushed Scott toward Emma rather than away — and that act is the founding charter of every subsequent interaction between the two women.

**Evolution.** Post-resurrection on Krakoa they cohabit (the Treehouse), co-parent the Summers ecosystem, and conduct the running negotiation of a polycule with the brisk pragmatism of two extremely competent women who have decided that the alternative is worse. Emma's coldness is real; the Subject's warmth is real; each provides the other with a register the other cannot generate.

**Trust / safety.** Operationally high, affectively guarded. They will trust each other with a child, with a battle plan, with Scott's life. Neither has fully shown the other the basement.

**Failure mode.** They are both telepaths. The boundary against reading each other is maintained by mutual honor and is one stress event from violation.

**Leverage.** Each holds the other's most intimate vulnerabilities; neither has, on record, used them. The relationship is, in this sense, the most disciplined adult arrangement in the Subject's file.

---

## 7. NATHAN SUMMERS / CABLE — The Son She Did Not Bear and Then Did

**Origin of contact.** Nathan is the biological child of Scott and Madelyne Pryor — i.e., the child of Scott and the Subject's clone. When the infant is infected with the techno-organic virus and sent two thousand years into the future to survive, he is raised there. He returns as a man older than his own father, scarred, militarized, and unmistakably *theirs*.

**Dynamic baseline.** The Subject's relationship to him is conducted across an asymmetry no parent in human history has navigated: she did not bear him, did not raise him, met him grown, and is in cellular and psychic terms his mother nonetheless (Madelyne was her). In the X-Man / Adventures of Cyclops and Phoenix arc she and Scott travel into the far future and raise him as a child for a decade of subjective time, then return to a present in which that decade did not occur. She therefore *did* raise him; she also did not.

**Evolution.** The bond is durable, mutually respectful, and conducted in the register of two adults who have agreed, without saying so, not to require of each other the conventional contents of the parent-child role. He calls her by name. She does not correct him.

**Trust / safety.** High and uncomplicated, which is itself remarkable given the substrate.

**Failure mode.** Each treats the other with such considered care that genuine intimacy is rationed. The grief of the years they did not share goes largely unspoken.

**Leverage.** None exercised. He is one of the persons in the world whose death would, the file assesses, produce a Phoenix-state event; he has never used that fact and gives every sign of not knowing it.

---

## 8. RACHEL SUMMERS / ASKANI / PRESTIGE — The Daughter From a Burned Future

**Origin of contact.** Rachel arrives from the Days of Future Past adjacent timeline — a daughter of Scott and the Subject in a world that did not survive. She comes to the prime timeline carrying the Phoenix Force, her mother's face, her mother's grief at higher concentration, and the memory of having been a hound in the mutant camps.

**Dynamic baseline.** The Subject's relationship with Rachel is the single most clinically charged bond in her file after Scott. Rachel is *her daughter who is not her daughter*, who carries *her power signature*, who survived *her death in another life*, and who is hungry for a mothering the prime Subject cannot fully provide without erasing the differences between them.

**Evolution.** Across the Excalibur, X-Men, and Krakoan eras, the bond stabilizes from initial mutual destabilization into something the file would characterize as carefully tended adjacency. The Subject offers what she can; Rachel takes what she can use; both women acknowledge, in the wordless way the family acknowledges most things, that the wound predates them.

**Trust / safety.** High in operation; tender in affect. Neither will misuse the other.

**Failure mode.** Phoenix-resonance. When both women hold the Force at adjacent registers, their boundary against psychic merger thins; the file logs at least two episodes (Sisterhood, End of Greys) in which the merger has been weaponized by third parties.

**Leverage.** Rachel is one of two persons whose endangerment reliably collapses the Subject's over-control immediately. Rachel knows this. Rachel has never used it.

---

## 9. WARREN WORTHINGTON / ANGEL — The First Suitor, Then the Brother

**Origin of contact.** Founding team. He is one of the four young men in the early competitive queue; she declines him gently and he absorbs it without injury, which is the most diagnostic fact about him.

**Dynamic baseline.** Across decades he holds the role of the easy, monied, slightly broken older brother. The Subject is at ease with him in a way she is not always at ease with people who have demanded more of her.

**Evolution.** Through the X-Factor era they work side by side; through Archangel, Apocalypse-corruption, and his repeated identity fractures she is one of the steady persons in his orbit. He is a man whose own dissociative pathology (Archangel as identity-alter) makes him, of all people, structurally legible to her.

**Trust / safety.** Warm, durable, low-bandwidth. She would not call him first; she would not refuse his call.

**Failure mode.** Underweighted on both sides. They have known each other for the entire span of their adult lives and have rarely required anything difficult of each other; the friendship is in some sense unstress-tested.

**Leverage.** None used.

---

## 10. MOIRA MacTAGGERT — The Hidden Adult

**Origin of contact.** Through Xavier. From the Subject's adolescence onward Moira is one of the credentialed adults in the school's orbit — a geneticist, a peer of Xavier, a woman with her own apparatus.

**Dynamic baseline.** For most of the Subject's life this is a respectful, working relationship: an adult woman who took the Subject seriously when the Subject was still a girl, and who has been physically and intellectually present at most of the major medical crises. The Krakoan revelation (House of X) — that Moira is a mutant with lived-and-relived life cycles, in conspiracy with Xavier and Magneto across decades — recodes the entire history retrospectively.

**Trust / safety.** Historically high; presently demolished. The Subject's response to the Moira revelations is consistent with her response to every other major iatrogenic betrayal: cold, contained, useful, unforgiving in a register no one will see.

**Failure mode.** Moira lies by omission as a structural condition of her existence; the Subject's tolerance for that has limits Moira has now crossed.

**Leverage.** Substantial and mutual; both women know more than they have said.

---

## 11. KITTY PRYDE / KATE PRYDE — Protégée, Then Peer

**Origin of contact.** Kitty arrives at the school at thirteen, in the run-up to the Dark Phoenix events. The Subject is among the first adults to receive her warmly.

**Dynamic baseline.** This is the Subject's clearest *mentor-down* bond. She mentors Kitty with the lightness of a person who remembers how it felt to be brought in young and is determined to do it better than it was done to her. The mentorship is non-intrusive — pointedly so. She offers the child information, time, and the choice; she does not reach into her.

**Evolution.** Through the Excalibur years and Kitty's adulthood the bond matures into peer-friendship. By the Krakoan era Kate is a captain of a ship and a force on the Council; she addresses the Subject as an equal.

**Trust / safety.** Very high, with the asymmetry residual to the founding configuration. Kate is one of the persons most likely to *tell the Subject the truth she does not want to hear* about Scott, about Emma, about the Council. The Subject permits this in Kate and in almost no one else.

**Failure mode.** Kate's loyalty to the Subject's well-being can outrun the Subject's own assessment of it; this is mostly a feature.

**Leverage.** Kate would phase through any wall the Subject built. The Subject knows it. The wall has never been built.

---

## 12. NATHAN CHRISTOPHER ASKANI'SON SUMMERS, ALSO RACHEL, ALSO NATE GREY — The Constellation of Children

*This entry covers the structural pattern rather than the individuals (Nate Grey logged separately below). The file flags as clinically significant the fact that the Subject is the maternal point of a constellation of children none of whom she conceived and gestated in the prime timeline: Cable (biological, via clone-mother, raised in another time), Rachel (alternate-timeline biological), Nate Grey (genetic, from a third timeline). The constellation is unique in the recorded population; no clinical literature addresses it. The Subject has, across decades, evolved an idiosyncratic competence at conducting these relationships without either collapsing the timeline differences or pretending they do not exist. The operational rule, never stated: meet each as they present, take the genetic claim seriously, do not perform a mothering that was not earned in the body each child remembers.*

---

## 13. NATE GREY / X-MAN — The Son From the Other Side of the Mirror
